## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of reactant concentration dA/dt as a function of time t and concentration A, which is the fundamental problem in chemical kinetics rate law identification. The rate law encodes the reaction mechanism.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (radioactive decay, simple decomposition)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (bimolecular reaction with single species)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate law)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse reaction with equilibrium)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme-catalyzed or saturation kinetics)
- Autocatalytic: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic-type autocatalysis)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A**2) (substrate inhibition)
- Mixed-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A)**2 (complex enzyme mechanism)
- Time-dependent forcing: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (externally driven reaction)
- Cooperative kinetics (Hill): dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (c2 + A**c1) (cooperative binding/reaction)
- Quadratic rate with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 + c1 * A + c2 (combined order kinetics)
- Langmuir-Hinshelwood: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A)**2 (surface-catalyzed reaction)
- Damped rate: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (time-dependent rate constant, e.g., catalyst deactivation)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Pure concentration dependence (no explicit t) suggests an autonomous ODE rate law from a well-defined reaction mechanism
- Explicit time dependence in dA/dt suggests external forcing, catalyst deactivation, or a reduced/eliminated intermediate variable
- Rational functions of A (e.g., A/(c+A)) indicate enzyme-like saturation or surface adsorption mechanisms
- Product terms A*(c-A) indicate autocatalytic or logistic growth where a conserved total concentration constrains the system
- Negative coefficients on concentration terms indicate consumption/decay while positive terms indicate production or reverse reactions
- Half-integer or fractional powers of A (e.g., A**0.5) suggest chain reaction mechanisms with radical intermediates
- Square of concentration in denominator (1+A)^2 suggests competitive or uncompetitive inhibition in catalytic systems
- Multiple additive rate terms with different powers of A suggest parallel reaction pathways or competing mechanisms
